<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.24084"></a>
<h1>Welcome</h1>
<p><img src="/media/media_52830_en.jpg"
alt="St Andrew's Building"
title="St Andrew's Building"
class=""
style="width : 280px; height : 200px; border : 0; padding : 4px; margin : ; float : right;  " />The Department of Religious Education is one of the largest, most innovative and exciting teaching and research&nbsp;departments of its kind in Britain. Its work embraces Religious Education in both religious and secular schools as well as the study of religion, politics, education, philosophy, theology and culture. There is wide staff expertise in the fields of anthropology, ethnography and sociology as well as philosophy of religion, philosophy of education, theology and cultural&nbsp;studies.</p>
<p>Programmes on offer include undergraduate and initial teacher education degrees and diplomas, Postgraduate Certificates, Masters,&nbsp;PhD and EdD. We also collaborate with other departments in the university in providing courses in teaching philosophy. Particular expertise is to be found in the study of religions in the context of Catholic education and schooling.</p>
<p>The Department is committed to being at the leading edge of international developments in the fields of Religious Education, Philosophy in education, Religious Schooling (including Catholic Schooling) and Moral and Citizenship Education. This issues in the highest quality teaching, research and scholarship as well as flagship initiatives in continuing professional development.</p>
<p>Through its programmes of initial teacher education, the Faculty of Education is recognised as the major provider of teachers for Catholic schools in Scotland. The Department therefore retains an important responsibility for the preparation of those teachers intending to work in Catholic schools and to teach Religious Education within them. This responsibility&nbsp;is discharged through a network of partnerships with Catholic Education and also in the continuing professional development of all staff active in the Catholic sector.</p>
<p>Enjoy browsing our website and if you wish for more information please donâ€™t hesitate to contact us.</p>
<p class="textsplash">The text from the&nbsp;8th Annual&nbsp;Cardinal Winning Lecture is available&nbsp;here <a href="/media/media_107664_en.pdf" target="_blank">Text of Cardinal Winning Lecture 2009</a></p>
<p class="textsplash"><a href="/media/media_112245_en.pdf" target="_blank">LOGOS Lent 09</a> - Read our latest edition of our electronic newsletter.</p>
<p class="textsplash">Courses coming&nbsp;in 2009, a Religious Education pathway through the MEd.&nbsp; </p>
<p></p>

<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.6908"></a>
<h1>Educational Studies</h1>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img src="/media/media_3297_en.jpg"
alt="Male and female student sitting on wall with University tower in background"
title="Male and female student sitting on wall with University tower in background"
class=""
style="width : 300px; height : 200px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " /> <br /></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>Welcome to Department of Educational Studies</strong>,</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Since the merger between the University of Glasgow's Department of Education&nbsp;and&nbsp;St Andrew's College in 1999, the Department of Educational Studies has come a long&nbsp;way. The Department is continuing to grow, building on our strengths and moving into&nbsp;the new areas that will be crucial to the success of knowledge-based societies in the&nbsp;twenty-first century, and we aim to become an international centre of learning. </p>
<p>The Department continues to raise its profile on international educational issues, covering&nbsp;&nbsp; all aspects of learning, from pre-5 to adult continuing education. The Educational Studies staff have important national and international connections and work closely with a range of organisations in Glasgow and across Scotland, indeed, this session has seen both the Department and Faculty attract high profile educational thinkers for keynotes, lectures and seminars demonstrating our continually growing reputation and on the international stage. </p>
<p>Educational Studies offers courses leading to higher degrees in all areas of education and related aspects of professional practice. To respond to the professional and personal requirements of practitioners at all levels, part-time and distance learning courses have been added to the portfolio of full-time courses delivered. The Department has many postgraduate taught and research students from the UK and many overseas countries, offering students the benefits of teaching based on the most up to date research. Applications and enquiries are welcomed from students, both nationally and internationally.<br /></p>
<p>Whether you are considering becoming a student in the Faculty of Education or wish to find out more about the breadth of the activities, we hope you enjoy browsing our site. </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;"></p>
<address style="text-align: justify;"><strong></strong></address>
<address style="text-align: justify;"><address style="text-align: justify;"><a href="mailto:b.carrington@educ.gla.ac.uk" style="text-align: left;"></a></address>

<h1><a href="/departments/educationalstudies/news/">News</a></h1>
<h2><a href="/departments/educationalstudies/news/headline_88387_en.html">MA Primary Education</a></h2>
<p>A brand new concurrent programme of primary teacher education has now launched at the University's Dumfries campus. This programme is the MA in Primary Education, and is unique in a number of aspects.</p>
<h2><a href="/departments/educationalstudies/news/headline_88440_en.html">BA Childhood Practice</a></h2>
<p>A new programme has been approved to be delivered within the Faculty, commencing academic session 2008-2009. The BA Childhood Practice has been developed to enable students with experience of working in the field of childhood practice to meet the requirements of the Standard for Childhood Practice (QAA, 2007). </p>

      <div class="maincontent"><!-- InstanceBeginEditable name="text" -->
        <h1>Welcome</h1>
        <p>The Department of Adult and Continuing Education (DACE) is one of the 
          largest departments of its type in the UK academic sector. Established 
          more than fifty years ago it aims to provide learning opportunities 
          for adults in the West of Scotland and to widen access to University 
          education to the community at large. The programme is taught by its 
          own academic staff and by enlisting or co-operating with members of 
          other University departments and other qualified persons outside the 
          University. Teaching services are provided in as wide a range of subjects 
          to as many groups as resources allow. The Department is committed to 
          the maintenance of University quality and traditions of excellence in 
          all educational programmes that it offers or with which it is associated. 
          Its staff ensure quality through their own research and scholarship 
          and have special experience and/or training in initiating, designing, 
          promoting and teaching courses for adults.</p>
        <p>The Department also acts as a direct link between the University and a wide variety of external agencies, organisations and institutions involved in post-compulsory education and training.</p>
        <p>Key areas of activity of the Department include:</p>
        <ul>
          <li>Provision of general <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk:443/departments/adulteducation">continuing 
            education programmes for the public</a></li>
          <li>Part-time courses for credit leading to <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/certHE/index.htm">Certificate 
            of Higher Education</a></li>
          <li><a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/access/index.html"> 
            Access courses</a>: introduction to university study for mature students 
          </li>
          <li>Outreach programmes, targeted at socially excluded groups, undertaken 
            in partnership with a wide range of external bodies </li>
          <li><a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/pgrad/pghomepage.htm">Postgraduate 
            programmes</a> in the field of adult and continuing education </li>
          <li><a href="courses/bacd.htm">Degree programme</a> in community development.</li>
          <li><a href="counsellingskills/index.htm">Certificate in Counselling 
            Skills</a></li>
          <li><a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/adulteducation/cht/">Children's Hearings 
            Training Unit</a> provides training for Panel members and Safeguarders; 
          </li>
          <li><a href="http://www.projectstrada.org/v1/"> STRADA (Scottish Training 
            on Drugs and Alcohol)</a>: DACE is a partner in this with the University's 
            Centre for Drugs Misuse Research and the organisation DrugScope</li>
          <li><a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/research">Research</a> 
            in the area of adult education and lifelong learning.<br />
          </li>
        </ul>
        <p>&nbsp;</p>

title=""
class="right"
style="width : 350px; height : 224px; border : 0; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " /> <span><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0cm 0cm 0pt;"><span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en;">The Department of Curriculum Studies is at the heart of one of the largest centres for teacher education in the <country-region prefix="" st1 ns="" />
<place prefix="" st1 ns="" />United Kingdom</place /> </country-region />and</span> <span style="color: black; mso-bidi-font-size: 9.5pt;">offers a strongly interrelated model of educational practice which applies theoretical awareness and policy developments in nursery, primary and secondary schools.</span> <br />
<br />
<span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en;">Provision includes undergraduate and initial teacher education degrees and we contribute to continuing professional development programmes such as Postgraduate Certificates, Diplomas, Masters,&nbsp;PhD and EdD.<br />
<br /></span>
<span style="color: black; mso-bidi-font-size: 9.5pt;">We are also a leading postgraduate department which offers excellence in teaching, a </span>
<span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">challenging student-centred learning environment</span> <span style="color: black; mso-bidi-font-size: 9.5pt;">and involvement in </span>
<span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">leading-edge internationally-competitive research and scholarship. </span>
<span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en;">Please <a href="/departments/curriculumstudies/contactus/#d.en.38080">contact us</a> if you wish more information.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0cm 0cm 0pt;"><span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en;"></span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0cm 0cm 0pt;"><span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en;"></span>
<span lang="EN" style="color: black; mso-ansi-language: en;"><strong>Harry Blee</strong> (Head of Department)</span> </p></span>

        <div class="profilesplash">
           <h1>International students</h1>
<h3>A warm welcome</h3>
<p>Our diverse University community is something we are very proud of at Glasgow, providing a rich cultural, social and educational mix which appeals to students and staff from all over the world. By choosing to study here you will join students from over 100 different countries, making up 15% of our total student community; last year we welcomed around 3,000 international students.</p>
<p>To make your experience with us as fulfilling and enjoyable as possible, we provide strong support systems and specialist staff dedicated to your needs.</p>
<p>Whatever stage you are at in your studies, you will always find someone on hand to provide you with help, guidance and advice.</p>
<p>The city of Glasgow has a reputation throughout the world as a friendly and welcoming place with a vibrant cultural life; we are delighted that many of our students say the same about the University. We hope that you will take the time to find out for yourself and look forward to welcoming you to the University of Glasgow.</p>
        </div>
        <div class="profileleftcol">
           <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/international/inyourregion/"><img src="/media/media_71476_en.gif"
alt=""
title=""
class=""
style="width : 170px; height : 69px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " /></a> <h2>News and Events</h2>
<ul><li>Find out more about Glasgow life in our <a href="/media/media_118038_en.pdf" target="_blank">International Student Guide</a>&nbsp;(PDF) </li>
<li>Download our <a href="/media/media_106124_en.pdf" target="_blank">Travel Schedule</a> (PDF)&nbsp;to find out where University staff are visiting over the next few months </li>
<li><a href="/news/archive/2008/october/headline_94802_en.html">Lonely Planet names Glasgow as one of the world's top cities</a> </li></ul>
        </div>

        <div class="profilerightcol">
           <h1>Contact us</h1>
<p><strong>International Office</strong> <br />Student Services<br />The Fraser Building<br />65 Hillhead Street<br />University of Glasgow<br />Glasgow G12 8QQ<br />
<br />Tel: +44 (0) 141 330 6680<br />Fax: +44 (0) 141 330 4045<br />E-mail: <a href="mailto:international@gla.ac.uk">international@gla.ac.uk</a> </p><!--div style="background: rgb(189,210,238) 0% 50%; margin-bottom: 10px; -moz-background-clip: -moz-initial; -moz-background-origin: -moz-initial; -moz-background-inline-policy: -moz-initial; border: 1px solid rgb(137,168,212); padding: 5px;">
<h3>Course Spotlight: </h3>
<p><b>Master of Research in Medical and Veterinary Microbiology</b></p>
<p>A 48 week full-time course with a focus on: <span type="media" id="79635" mediaattributes="class%3D%22%22+width%3D%22%22+height%3D%22%22+border%3D%22%22+padding%3D%22%22+margin%3D%22%22+float%3D%22right%22+cp-enable%3D%22false%22+"><img src="SiteManager?ctfn=download&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;fnno=60&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;ceid=18749646"
alt=""
title=""
class=""
style="width : 175px; height : 98px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : right;  " /></span></p>
<ul><li>Molecular microbiology </li>
<li>Microbial pathogenesis </li>
<li>Epidemiology and evolutionary microbiology </li>
<li>Vaccine design and development </li></ul>Further information is available on the Graduate School of Biomedical and Life Sciences <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/faculties/fbls/gs/masterscourses/mresinmedicalveterinarymicrobiology/">website</a> and&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;nbsp;in the&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;nbsp;subject&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;nbsp;<a title="home &amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt; Postgraduate study &amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt; Download &amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt; brochures" href="SiteManager?ctfn=hierarchy&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;fnno=10&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;sid=3391">brochures</a> pdf download section.</div-->
        <br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:left;" />  
        </div>

<a name="d.en.66406"></a>
<h1>University of Glasgow International Educational Consultancy</h1>
<h2>Innovation in Learning</h2>
<p>The University of Glasgowâ€™s International Educational Consultancy is a specialist centre in the <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/faculties/education/index.html">Faculty of Education </a>working nationally and internationally with central government, education authorities, schools and other public bodies to improve the quality of education. </p>
<p><a href="/services/internationaleducationalconsultancy/professorkaylivingstondirector/">Professors Kay Livingston </a>and <a href="/services/internationaleducationalconsultancy/professorviviennebaumfielddirector/">Professor Vivienne Baumfield,</a> are the Directors of the International Educational Consultancy and they both have extensive experience of leading research and consultancy projects in the UK and in a number of countries around the world. Working with staff from the University they are able to design, organise and deliver research and professional development programmes to meet the demands of&nbsp; learning and teaching in the 21st century. </p>
<p>The staff have experience leading policy-related research and evaluation projects and providing consultancy in pedagogy, curriculum, leadership and organisational change. Areas of particular expertise include:</p>
<ul><li>International education </li>
<li>Intercultural education </li>
<li>Global citizenship </li>
<li>Teacher education </li>
<li>School improvement </li>
<li>School self-evaluation </li>
<li>Practitioner enquiry </li>
<li>Assessment </li>
<li>Values education </li>
<li>Drugs education </li>
<li>Parental involvement in education through home/school links </li>
<li>Technology in education </li>
<li>Science, engineering and mathematics</li></ul>
<h3 style="text-align: center;"><a href="/services/internationaleducationalconsultancy/contactus/">Contact us</a> for more information on how we can work together.</h3>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />

<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.76424"></a>
<h1>Accessibility</h1>
<h2>Equality and Diversity</h2>
<p>The University of Glasgow is committed to promoting equality in all its activities and aims to provide a work, learning, research and teaching environment free from discrimination and unfair treatment. We see inclusiveness as fundamental to our strategy and identity and recognise that increasing opportunities for all who want to engage with our community and facilities is a benefit to us.&nbsp; Further information is available from our <a href="/services/equalitydiversity/">Equality and Diversity Unit</a> </p>
<h2>Physical Access</h2>
<p><strong>DisabledGo</strong></p>
<p><a href="http://www.disabledgo.info/Education/Default.asp?TownID=152&ClassificationName=">DisabledGo</a> is a social enterprise who complete access audits for disabled users of public, private and voluntary sector buildings. They have completed an audit for the University which includes 80 services across the campus, including the Hunterian Museum, Sports and Recreation Service, Registry, various accommodation sites. </p>
<p><strong>Accessible maps</strong></p>
<p>The University has produced <a href="/about/locationmapsandtravel/mapsandtravel/maincampusmap/">accessible maps</a> for the main campus. These highlight where there are accessible parking spaces and toilets. </p>
<p><strong>Mobility Scooters</strong></p>
<p><a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/services/studentdisability/">Student Disability Service</a> has two mobility scooters available for students and staff for hire (no charge) for assistance in crossing the campus. Please contact the service directly to find out further details.</p>
<p>If you have experienced a particular issue with physical access anywhere on campus, please email <a href="mailto:physicalaccessissues@gla.ac.uk">physicalaccessissues@gla.ac.uk</a> where a member of Estates and Buildings staff will deal with your concern.</p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<h2>Web Accessibility</h2>
<p>The website of the University of Glasgow has been designed to be as accessible as possible.&nbsp; We do however welcome feedback on suggestions for improvements and any problems ecountered.&nbsp; Please mail <a href="mailto:webteam@gla.ac.uk">webteam@gla.ac.uk</a>.<strong></strong></p>
<p><strong>Standards compliance</strong></p>
<p>Our website design employs XHTML and CSS.&nbsp; We follow best practice guidelines, such as the W3C Web Content Accessibility Guidelines and PAS 78 (British Standards Institute guidance on website accessibility).<br /></p>
<p><strong>Resizable text</strong></p>
<p>All navigation and content text used on our website can be increased or decreased in size. Please see the BBC's <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/accessibility/">My Web My Way</a> -(accessibility features of browsers and operating systems) for assistance.<br /></p>


<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>

<h1>Funded research</h1>
<ul><li><a href="/faculties/education/research/currentresearchprojects/inter-lifeinteroperabilityandtransition/">ESRC/ESRC - Inter-Life: Interoperability and Transition</a> </li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/research/currentresearchprojects/doesreligioneducationwork/">AHRC/ESRC - Does religious education work?</a> </li>

<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.9795"></a>
<h1>Faculty of Education</h1>
<p>The Faculty of Education at the University of Glasgow is an exciting and stimulating place to study at both <a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/">undergraduate</a> and <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/">postgraduate</a> levels. New degree programmes include: <a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/primaryeducation/">BEd Honours in Primary Education</a>; the <a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/primaryeducationwithteachingqualificationdumfriescampus/">MA in Primary Education</a> offered on the Dumfries campus; the <a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/childhoodpractice/">BA in Childhood Practice</a>; and the <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/pgde/">PGDE one-year programme for primary and secondary education</a> which offers 90 Masters-level credits. It has a robust, active and expanding <a href="/faculties/education/research/">research</a> portfolio with international expertise in the areas of Adult and Lifelong Learning, Science Education, Teacher Education, Religion and Education, Social Justice and Globalisation and Education among others.</p>
<p>We will be pleased to hear from you and welcome your interest in the Faculty of Education at the University of Glasgow.</p>

<h1>Disclaimer</h1>
<p>The content of the University's main external website is overseen by the Web Team. At departmental and other levels, content is maintained locally. Whilst every attempt is made to ensure that information is accurate and up-to-date, some information is subject to change. The University will not be held liable for information that is subject to change and reserves the right to alter the content of the external website at any time.<br /></p><h3>Prospectuses<br /></h3>
<p>The Undergraduate and Postgraduate Prospectuses are intended to help you choose your course of study at the University of Glasgow. They do not replace the University Calendar as a statement of the University regulations. All students will be required as a condition of enrolment to abide by, and to submit to the procedures of, the University's rules and regulations, as amended from time to time. A copy of the current regulations is available at: <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/calendar">www.gla.ac.uk/calendar/</a> or on request, from the Registry: <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/registry/">www.gla.ac.uk/registry/</a>
<br />
<br />Every effort has been made to ensure the accuracy of the information contained within the prospectuses but it is subject to alteration without notice. The University will use all reasonable endeavours to deliver courses in accordance with the descriptions set out in the prospectuses. The University, however, reserves the right to make variations to the content or methods of delivery of courses, to discontinue courses and to merge or combine courses, if such action is reasonably considered to be necessary by the University. If the University discontinues any course, it will use reasonable endeavours to provide a suitable alternative course. In the event of industrial action or other circumstances beyond the control of the University that interferes with itsability to provide these courses or services, the University will undertake to minimise disruption as far as is practicable.<br />
<br />The online versions of the prospectuses are for guidance only.<br />
<br />Although these may contain more up to date material: such as newly announced courses of study or changes to contact details, the printed versions remain the definitive editions.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />

<h1>Intranet</h1>
<p>This section of the Faculty website is created to separate information which is mostly of interest to the internal University community from the public site.</p>
<p>Anyone who wishes to access these pages from home will need to use the University's <a href="/services/it/forstaff/flexiblenetworkaccess/">Virtual Private Network</a> (VPN) service. If you require VPN then please follow these <a href="/services/it/forstaff/flexiblenetworkaccess/offcampusaccess/">VPN instructions</a>. Please note that students do not need to register for the VPN service.<br /></p>

<a name="d.en.19123"></a>
<h1>Continuing Professional Development (CPD)</h1>
<p>The Faculty provides an extensive range of CPD opportunities for teachers and others involved in education. Our CPD is designed to be as flexible as possible, including daytime, twilight, weekend and vacation modes, and ranging from one-off courses to full programmes.</p>
<ul class="longlist"><li><a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/faculties/education/cpd/">CPD short courses</a>
<ul><li><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/pgcertinprofessionaldevelopmentineducation/">New Postgraduate Certificate Opportunities relating to Standard CPD Short Courses</a> </li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/">Taught postgraduate programmes</a> </li>
<li href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/courses/"><a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/courses/">DACE (Department of Adult and Continuing Education) courses</a></li>
<li href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/courses/"><a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/continuingprofessionaldevelopment/communitydevelopment/">Community Development one day courses</a></li></ul>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />

<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.108880"></a>
<h1>Childhood Practice</h1>
<h2>Degree : BA (Childhood Practice)</h2>
<p class="textsplash">This programme has been developed to enable students with experience
of working in childhood practice to meet the requirements of the
Standard for Childhood Practice (SSSC and QAA, 2007). The programme has
been designed to enable practitioners to gain an academic and
professional qualification whilst remaining in employment.</p>

<h2>What will I study?</h2>
<p>The programme contains work-based elements and will be rooted in
practice. You will review your experience and use this review as the
basis for planning and setting targets for professional development
within the programme.&nbsp; </p>
<p>Courses to be studied are dependant on your previous qualifications
(HNCs, PDAs and SVQs). In consultation with the programme leader, your
studies will be made up of the following courses.</p>
<p><strong>Core courses</strong>
<br /> </p>
<ul><li>Professional enquiry: the standard for childhood practice </li>
<li>Professional enquiry: planning a project </li>
<li>E-learning developments &amp; communication </li>
<li>Professional enquiry: taking action &amp; making an intervention </li>
<li>Professional enquiry: sustaining &amp; communicating improvements in practice </li>
<li>Leadership, management &amp; professional values<br /></li></ul>
<p>
<strong>Optional courses</strong>&nbsp;
</p>
<p></p>
<ul><li>Childhood practice: global perspectives </li>
<li>Self-evaluation &amp; quality management </li>
<li>Key issues &amp; debates in contemporary childhood </li>
<li>Multi-professional collaboration in children's services </li>
<li>Social &amp; cultural contexts of childhood </li>
<li>Practice placement</li></ul>
<h2>How will I learn?</h2>
<p>Teaching is delivered through a combination of lectures, work in
groups and other popular education methods. As this is a work-based
learning programme, in addition to formal learning, you will draw from
your own practice in the field of childhood practice. <br /></p>
<h2>Special features</h2>

<p>This degree has been designed to meet the registration requirements
of the Scottish Social Services Councilâ€™s for manager/lead practitioner
in day care services for children.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.108881"></a>
<h1>Childhood Practice Entry Requirements</h1>
<p>All students will be required to have an HNC, PDA, SVQ3, SVQ4 or
equivalent previous professional qualifications in Childrenâ€™s Care,
Learning and Development or Playwork. Students are accepted onto this
programme through providing evidence of their relevant work experience
and readiness to enter higher education. All students will be expected
to be employed in professional roles within the field of Childhood
Practice.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.108882"></a>
<h1>What are my career prospects?</h1>
<p>The programme will allow those in leadership roles, and aspiring
leaders, in childhood practice settings to progress their personal and
professional development. The programme will be delivered in a way that
can enable learners to take forward their professional development,
irrespective of their professional background.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.120477"></a>
<h1>Find out more</h1>
<p>For further information, please contact:<br /></p>
<p><strong></strong>Mr Kevin M Kelman<br />

<h1>Undergraduate study</h1>
<p><strong>A degree from Glasgow is one of the most sought after in the
world: weâ€™ve trained teachers from Manchester to Malawi, from Surrey to
South Africa.</strong></p>
<p>Undergraduate degree programmes: </p>

<ul><li><a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/childhoodpractice/">Childhood Practice</a></li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/communitydevelopment/">Community Development</a></li>

<a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/technologicaleducation/"> </a></li>

<p>The Faculty also offers courses leading to the Certificate of Higher Education which is a University level award for a programme of learning that is usually 
            taken by part-time study.</p>

<ul><li><a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/">Undergraduate study</a></li>

<a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/"><img src="/media/media_20218_en.gif"
alt="Graduate School for Education"
title="Graduate School for Education"
class=""
style="width : 140px; height : 25px; border : 0; padding : 4; margin : ; float : ;  " /></a>
<br />
</div>
<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.18631"></a>
<h1>Programmes and Courses</h1>
<p>The Faculty of Education is an exciting and stimulating place to study at both <a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/">undergraduate</a> and postgraduate levels. It has a robust, active and expanding research portfolio with international expertise in the areas of adult &amp; lifelong learning, science education, teacher education, religion &amp; education, social justice and globalisation &amp; education among others.</p>
<p>Through the <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/">Graduate School for Education</a> we offer a range of taught postgraduate degrees, designed for a broad cross-section of interests. For those of you wishing to gain deeper insight and reflection on your own education practice we offer a suite of tailor made programmes, aimed at providing the necessary qualifications and skills for your professional life.</p>
<p>Our broad range of programmes include provision for those wishing to be teachers; those wishing to enhance and develop their professional skills through continuing professional development; those wishing to teach in community education and those wishing to undertake research. We offer creative and innovative online courses including a Doctorate in Education.</p>
<p>Faculty staff are actively involved in a wide variety of external networks. Consequently the faculty is well placed to promote a dynamic interaction with policy makers and practitioners in relation to the generation of research questions, the conduct of research and the dissemination of research findings. These activities feed directly into the wide range of taught postgraduate programmes offered in the faculty.</p>
<p>With the shift towards a global, knowledge-based economy, the promotion of education within a lifelong learning context forms a key feature of strategies aimed at the achievement of social and economic policies. The Faculty of Education is a future-oriented institution with a strong past. We have major research strengths in science education where the current director of the Centre for Science Education recently received the Royal Society of Chemistry's Nyholm Medal for an outstanding contribution to science education.</p>
<p>Our <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/index.html">adult and lifelong learning</a> work figures among the very best in the UK and beyond. Leadership and management, and support for learning are also important areas of excellence. Our work in faith-based schooling is among the most thoughtful and innovative in and beyond the UK. All of this work and much more besides is developed within the orbit of our over riding commitment to social justice. Currently we house a Department for International Development funded unit on global citizenship. Our Scottish Centre for Research in Education is the oldest such centre in the UK and conducts research for government, the EU and other agencies. We have recently appointed two new professors of international standing to strengthen our team.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>

<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.102165"></a>
<h1>Education (Primary/Secondary)</h1>
<p class="textsplash">Departmental information: : 
<br />Admissions Secretary<br />Tel: +44 (0)141 330 2463/3467<br />Email: <a href="mailto:admissions@educ.gla.ac.uk">admissions@educ.gla.ac.uk</a></p>
<ul><li><strong>Postgraduate Diploma in Education (PGDE</strong>): 10 months full-time<strong></strong>
<br /></li></ul>
<p>
This new PGDE programme is a Masters-level qualification in teacher education. As well as offering courses in educational and curricular issues, the programme also highlights the importance of practitioner enquiry. It is this systematic reflection on teaching in the classroom which gives the programme its distinctive Masters character. Taken together, the courses are designed to equip teachers with the knowledge, skills and values they need to become the committed professionals necessary for todayâ€™s schools. The programme consists of 18 weeks of study in the faculty and 18 weeks of school experience in our partner schools. Within the programme there are separate pathways for qualification as a primary teacher or as a secondary teacher.</p>
<h2>Content </h2>
<p><strong>The programme will prepare you to meet the demands of the profession through the following areas of study:</strong> </p>
<ul><li>Understanding learning &amp; teaching</li>
<li>Learning &amp; teaching in the primary curriculum OR Learning &amp; teaching in the secondary curriculum</li>
<li>Evaluating learning &amp; teaching</li>
<li>Religious education (students who complete this course will be awarded the Catholic Teacherâ€™s Certificate in Religious Education).</li></ul>

<p><strong>Secondary teaching qualifications are offered in the following subjects:</strong> </p>
<ul><li>Art and design</li>
<li>Biology<br /></li>
<li>Business education</li>
<li>Chemistry<br /></li>
<li>Computing</li>
<li>English</li>
<li>English and Classics</li>
<li>Geography</li>
<li>History</li>
<li>History and Classics</li>
<li>History and Modern studies<br /></li>
<li>Mathematics</li>
<li>Mathematics and Computing</li>
<li>Mathematics and Physics<br /></li>
<li>Modern languages (French, French with Spanish, French with Italian, French with German, Spanish with French)</li>
<li>Modern studies</li>
<li>Modern studies and History</li>
<li>Physics<br /></li>
<li>Religious education. <br /></li></ul>
<br />
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="twocolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.88909"></a>
<h1>PGDE (Primary) entry requirements</h1>
<p>Entrance to the programme is based on academic qualifications, relevant work experience and performance at interview. The academic entry requirements for 2009 entry for this programme are:</p>
<ul><li>a degree from a UK university (including non-Honours/ordinary degrees) or an alternative degree qualification approved by the General Teaching Council for Scotland, and</li><li>Higher English at Grade C or above, and</li><li>Standard Grade Mathematics at Grade 1 or 2</li></ul>
<p>Acceptable alternative qualifications in English:</p>
<ul><li>Communications 4 and Literature 1</li><li>GCSE English Language and GCSE English Literature at Grade C or above</li>
<li>Irish Leaving Certificate Higher English at Grade C3 or above</li></ul>
<p>Acceptable alternative qualifications in Mathematics:</p>
<ul><li>Intermediate Level 2 Mathematics at Grade C or above</li>
<li>GCSE Mathematics at Grade B or above</li>
<li>Irish Leaving Certificate Ordinary Mathematics at Grade B3 or above<br /></li></ul>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.88910"></a>
<h1>PGDE (Secondary) entry requirements</h1>
<p>Entrance to the programme is based on academic qualifications and
performance at interview. The academic entry requirements for 2009
entry for this programme are:</p>
<ul><li>a degree from a UK university (including non-Honours/ordinary
degrees) or an alternative degree qualification approved by the General
Teaching Council for Scotland. The degree should contain 80 credit
points overall in the subject which you intend to teach, of which 40
must be at Year 2 level or above. See <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/pgde/#d.en.88911">PGDE Secondary Education Degree Requirements</a> for specific subject requirements, and</li>
<li>Higher English at Grade C or above</li></ul>
<p>Acceptable alternative qualifications in English:</p>
<ul><li>Communications 4 and Literature 1</li>
<li>GCSE English Language and GCSE English Literature at Grade C or above</li>
<li>Irish Leaving Certificate Higher English at Grade C3 or above
  </li></ul>

<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.88911"></a>
<h1>PGDE Secondary Education Degree Requirements</h1>
<p>The degree requirements for the PGDE Secondary Education are based
on credits â€“ this is because credits are standard across all Scottish
Universities. A credit point is a measure of the amount of learning you
have done. To find out more about the credit point breakdown of your
degree, look at your degree transcript.</p>
<p>The degree should normally contain 80 credit points relevant to the
subject you want to teach, including 40 credit points at second year
undergraduate level or above.&nbsp; However, some subjects have very
specific demands.</p>
<h2>PGDE Secondary Education Subjects with Specific Requirements</h2>
<p>The following subjects have specific requirements:</p>
<p>
<strong>Art &amp; Design</strong>
</p>
<p>You will need good academic grades and a degree with at least 80
credit points from a range of the following practical subjects:
Drawing, Painting, Sculpture, Model Making, Printmaking, Textiles,
Photography and Environmental Art. </p>
<p>
<strong>Business Education</strong>
<br />You will need a degree with at least 80 credit points from a range
of the following subjects: Accounting, Economics, Information
Technology and Business Management.</p>
<p>You will also need to demonstrate a sound knowledge of Office &amp; Information Management.</p>
<p>
<strong>Classics</strong>
</p>
<p>To teach Classical Studies, you will need 80 credit points from the
following: Ancient History, Classical Archaeology, Classical
Civilisation or Classical Studies.</p>
<p>
<strong>Computing</strong>
</p>
<p>You will need a degree with 80 credit points, 40 of these credit
points must be at Year 2 Level or above from at least two of the
following: Computer Systems, Software Development, Databases or
Information Systems. </p>
<p>You will also need 40 credits in a computing subject relevant to the Computing curriculum taught in Scottish schools. </p>
<p>

<strong>English</strong>
</p>
<p>You will need a degree with at least 80 credit points in English.
At least 40 of these credit points must be in English or Scottish
Literature.</p>
<p>
<strong>Mathematics</strong>
</p>
<p>You will need a degree with at least 80 credit points of maths
related subject such as Algebra, Analysis, Calculus, Geometry,
Statistics, Differential Equations or Probability.</p>
<p>

<strong>Modern Foreign Languages</strong>
</p>
<p>1) Entry requirements for first language:</p>
<ul><li>a degree with at least 80 credit points in the first language you want to teach </li>
<li>before starting the course, you must have lived for six months in a country where the language is spoken </li>
<li>you will have to prove to the university that you are competent at speaking the language </li></ul>

<p>The scope of your language degree must allow you to
contribute to wider programmes of study in schools â€“ such as
literature, cultural studies, area studies or languages in work.</p>

<p>While you lived abroad, you must have taken full part in
the language and culture of the country. You must normally have lived
in the country for blocks of at least three months. So if you have
spent one of your study years abroad, you will be fine.</p>

<p>2) Entry requirements for second languages:a degree with at least 80 credit points in the second language you want to teach</p>

<ul><li>before starting the course, you must have lived for at least three months in a country where the language is spoken </li>
<li>you will have to prove to the university that you are competent at speaking the language </li></ul>
<p>Of course, you will also meet all the requirements for your first foreign language.</p>
<p>The scope of your language degree must allow you to
contribute to wider programmes of study in schools â€“ such as
literature, cultural studies, area studies or languages in work.</p>
<p>While you lived abroad you must have taken full part in the
language and culture of the country. You must normally have lived in
the country for a block of at least three months. </p>
<p>Please note that you must have lived in the country where
the second language is spoken for a full six months before you can get
full registration with the General Teaching Council for Scotland
(GTCS). If you have any questions about the registration and residency
requirements for second languages, get in touch with the GTCS.</p>

<p>3) Native speakers of a modern foreign language:
</p>
<p>If you are a native speaker of a modern foreign language
and you have a degree in your own language, you may be qualified to
train to teach that language. Your degree must meet the requirements
outlined above (entry requirements for first language).</p>
<p>If you are a native speaker and have a degree in an
additional language which meets these requirements, you may train to
teach that language as well as your mother tongue. For example, a
French student with a degree in German can train to teach German and
French.</p>
<p><strong>Modern Studies</strong></p>
<p>You must have a degree with at least 80 credit points from two of
the subjects listed below. Within these 80 credit points at least 40
must be from either Politics or Sociology. </p>
<ul><li>Economics </li>
<li>Geography </li>
<li>History or Economic History </li>
<li>International Relations </li>
<li>Politics </li>
<li>Sociology </li>
<li>Social Policy</li></ul>
<p><strong>Physics</strong></p>
<p>You will need a degree with at least 80 credit points from a range
of the following subjects: Electricity and Magnetism, Electronics,
Optics, Mechanics, Dynamics, Nuclear and Atomic Physics.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.99521"></a>
<h1>Application procedure</h1>
<p> Applications for the PGDE programme must be made online through the <a href="http://www.gttr.ac.uk">Graduate Teacher Training Registry</a> (GTTR) website.</p>
<p>Please contact the <strong>Admissions Secretary</strong> for further information.</p>
<p><strong>Telephone: +44 (0)141 330 2463<br />Email: <a href="mailto:admissions@educ.gla.ac.uk">admissions@educ.gla.ac.uk</a></strong></p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>

<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.17362"></a>
<h1>Welcome</h1>
<p>Welcome to the Graduate School for Education. Our aim is to foster research in education through <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/">taught Masters programmes,</a> our flagship professional doctorate <a href="/departments/educationalstudies/postgraduatestudies/doctorateineducationedd/">(EdD)</a> and through <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/researchprogrammes/">PhDs by research</a>, including a joint <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/researchprogrammes/jointphd/">Glasgow/Taiwan PhD Programme in Education.</a></p>
<p>Currently there are over&nbsp;a hundred&nbsp;research students studying towards research masters and doctoral awards on a full and part-time basis. <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/currentstudents/researchstudents/">Find out what they are doing</a></p>
<p>The Graduate School is proud to welcome students from as far a field as Oman and Taiwan, Malawi and Poland as well as those from the immediate locality. This global mix of home and international students provides an exciting environment to study and socialise.&nbsp; </p>
<p>The Faculty has recently celebrated a record number of&nbsp; home and international students graduating with a PhD. <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/graduatingstudents/">Read more </a>about their experience and what they are doing now.</p>
<div class="newsbox_blue"><p class="textsplash_blue"><strong>News And Events</strong></p>
<ul class="longlist"><li><strong><a href="http://education.moodle.gla.ac.uk/course/view.php?id=1485" target="_blank">Induction and Welcome for Postgraduate Research Students<br /></a></strong>Calling all new and returning research students! &nbsp;Please register now for the Induction Day on 15th October.</li>
<li><strong><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/induction/">Postgraduate Induction Week<br /></a></strong>The postgraduate induction week for students on taught courses&nbsp;will take place from Saturday 12th to Saturday 19th September 2009. </li>
<li><strong><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/pgdipchildhooddevelopment/#d.en.125605">PG Diploma in Childhood </a></strong>
<strong><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/pgdipchildhooddevelopment/#d.en.125605">Practice</a> <br /></strong>This innovative new programme is currently undergoing approval and accreditation by SSSC. Applications are invited for session 2009 </li>
<li><strong><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/mscorganisationalleadership/">MSc Organisational Leadership - Revised!</a></strong> <br />This programme has been revised under the leadership of Prof Tony Townsend applications are invited for session 2009/10 </li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/events/escalate/"><strong>ESCalate Conference</strong></a> <br />Staff and students from the Faculty&nbsp;make&nbsp;their way&nbsp;to Birmingham to support the Dean and fellow student Angela Japp&nbsp;who were presenting at the conference.&nbsp; </li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/events/internationalweekend/"><strong>Faculty Away Weekend</strong> </a>
<br />Some Thoughts developed at the Education Faculty Weekend Away to discuss the Theme: Glasgow University as an International Space</li></ul></div>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>

<h1>UCAS CODES</h1>
<ul><li>EDUCATION WITH PRIMARY TEACHING QUALIFICATION: X123</li></ul>
<p><img src="/media/media_118330_en.gif"
alt="pdf download"
title="pdf download"
class="right"
style="width : 14px; height : 16px; border : 0; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " />
<a href="http://senate.gla.ac.uk/progspecs/MA_Hons_Primary_Educ_with_Teaching_Qual.pdf">Primary Education with Teaching Qualification Programme Specification</a>
<br /></p>
</div>
<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.108871"></a>
<h1>Primary Education with Teaching Qualification  <span class="hideindumfries">(Dumfries Campus)</span></h1>
<h2>Degree: MA (Hons)<br /></h2>

<p><strong>The MA Primary Education with Teaching Qualification was given
unconditional approval by the General Teaching Council for Scotland on
the 7th August 2008.</strong></p>
<p class="textsplash">This new four-year degree programme offers prospective primary
teachers the opportunity to learn with students on other degree
programmes at the University of Glasgow, Dumfries Campus. You will gain
a primary teaching qualification and develop transferable skills,
including a professional approach and independence, which will prepare
you for the role of the primary teacher.</p>
<h2>What can I expect to study?</h2>
<p>As well as studying a combination of the courses from the MA Liberal Arts Programme, you will also follow a programme involving:</p>
<h3>Curriculum studies</h3>

<p>These courses develop the knowledge, understanding and skills of the main areas of the primary school curriculum.</p>
<p>You will benefit from the research expertise and teaching strengths of resident Dumfries Campus staff in the areas of<br /></p>
<ul><li>&nbsp; </li>
<li> </li>
<li> (history, literature, modern languages, philosophy and science and technology).<br /></li></ul>
<p>In addition the Liberal Arts ethos develops a rigorous, self-reliant
and creative approach to learning while encouraging good academic
practice and active citizenship: highly relevant to the new Curriculum
for Excellence 3-18.<br /></p>
<h3>Educational studies</h3>
<p>These courses develop the knowledge, skills and understanding for
effective learning, teaching, assessment and reporting in the
classroom, as well as encouraging the pastoral and support role a
teacher in a primary school undertakes. You will also acquire
up-to-date knowledge and understanding of national policy and
curricular developments.<br /></p>
<h3>School experience</h3>
<p>This element of the programme aims to develop your awareness of all
aspects of the work and organisation of the primary school. At least 30
weeks of the four-year programme will be spent working in schools. This
will take the form of single or serial days in the early stages of the
programme, developing into block placements of several weeks. </p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="twocolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.110432"></a>
<h1>Entry requirements</h1>
<h2>Typical offer </h2>
<p></p>
<ul><li><strong>Highers</strong>: AAB or BBBB<br /></li>
<li><strong>A-levels</strong>: BBB<br /></li></ul>
<p>Full details of : <br /></p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.108872"></a>
<h1>What are my career prospects?</h1>
<p>Primary teaching is a highly valued, people-centred profession.
Primary teachers not only contribute to the education and development
of their pupils but also make a wider contribution to schools and local
communities. </p>
<p>After qualification, new teachers are guaranteed one full yearâ€™s
employment to complete their probationary period. Thereafter,
continuing professional development is supported by employers and other
course providers. There are opportunities for development in leadership
and management, specialist subject study areas and for further
postgraduate study and research.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>

<h1>Find out more</h1>
<p>For further information, or the opportunity to visit the Dumfries Campus, please contact:</p>
<p>

<h1>UCAS CODES</h1>
<ul><li>PRIMARY EDUCATION: X120 </li>
<li>PRIMARY EDUCATION (Dumfries Campus): X123</li></ul>
</div>
<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.108865"></a>
<h1>Primary Education</h1>
<h2>Degree: BEd</h2>
<p class="textsplash">
This degree programme qualifies you to teach children aged 3-12 years.</p>
<h2>What will I study?</h2>You will take the following courses in years one and two:<br />
<br />
<ul><li>Educational Values form the backbone of the degree structure. In year one you will take courses in Educational Values for the Self and Educational Values for Self, School and Society with a focus on the child. In year two you will take courses in Educational Values for the Teacher and Educational Values through the Curriculum. Embedded within these courses will be opportunities for undertaking serial field experiences and block field experiences.</li></ul>
<br />
<ul><li>Learning How to Learn and Learning How Others Learn are aimed at developing your academic and communication skills along with your intellectual abilities in order to fully engage in your coursework.</li></ul>
<br />
<ul><li>You will select a Liberal Arts elective in year one and year two. These will allow you to study a broader range of disciplines and contribute to your own professional and intellectual development. </li></ul>
<br />
<ul><li>You will also study a course in Religious Education. In keeping with the Faculty of Educationâ€™s mission, this course is rooted in the traditions of Catholic Christianity with a focus in years one and two on the study of theology.</li></ul>
<br />In years three and four you will be involved in developing your skills and abilities as an emerging professional committed to lifelong development through overarching courses on Curriculum Development, Educational Change and The Emerging Enquiring Professional.<br />
<br />
<strong>Field experience</strong>
<br />
This involves developing an awareness of all aspects of the work and organisation of the primary school. At least 32 weeks of the four-year programme will be spent working in schools. This will take the form of single or serial days in the early stages of the programme and will develop into block placements of several weeks in schools.&nbsp; Ultimately, you will take responsibility for a considerable part of the work of a class.<br />
<br />You will have the opportunity to undertake placements in all stages of the primary school and also in a nursery school. In fourth year, you will be able to choose the stage for your placement. Additionally, you will be developing your knowledge and understanding of how schools, as organisations, are managed and operate.&nbsp; School experience is central to the programme and provides a focus for the various areas of the programme.<br />
<br />
<h2>How will I learn?</h2>
<p>Teaching is delivered through a combination of lectures, small group
tutorials and seminars and you will develop understanding, skills and
expertise in working in the school classroom through school experience.
You will have the opportunity to teach at the various levels within a
primary school. Field experience occurs in every year of the programme.
You will spend the equivalent of one academic year working in schools.</p>
<h2>Special features</h2>
<ul><li>This programme leads to registration with the General Teaching Council for Scotland.</li>
<li>Religious and moral education is a key component in primary
education in Scotland in all schools. Catholic students who complete
the appropriate course in Religious Education will be awarded the
Catholic Teacherâ€™s Certificate in Religious Education.</li></ul>
<h2>Note</h2>
<p>The Scottish Government expects the Faculty of Education to provide
adequate numbers of teachers to teach in Catholic schools in Scotland.
This particular programme provides support for, and emphasis on, the
initial teacher education of those who intend to teach in Catholic
schools. The design of the programme necessarily reflects the
denominational sector requirements and prospective applicants should
consider this before applying. The faculty welcomes applications from
all qualified candidates. In the selection procedures for interview,
priority is given to those who indicate, in their personal statement,
their intention to teach in Catholic schools and to seek the Catholic
Teacherâ€™s Certificate in Religious Education.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="twocolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

<p></p>

<li><strong>A-levels</strong>: BBB<br /></li></ul>
<p>Full details of : <br /></p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />

<div class="onecolclear"></div><div class="links" style="display:none;">

</div>
<div class="maincontent"  style="margin-right:0">
<a name="d.en.108866"></a>
<h1>What are my career prospects?</h1>
<p>Home/EU graduates are eligible for one yearâ€™s induction experience in a
Scottish primary school. It is expected that there will be an
increasing demand for new entrants to the teaching profession in
primary schools in Scotland and elsewhere. Once in the profession,
promotion will be determined by your professionalism, enthusiasm,
continued professional development and willingness to take on more
responsibility. Opportunities exist for career progression within
schools and more widely in posts such as HM inspector and education
adviser.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>

<h1>St Andrew's Building</h1>
<p><img src="/media/media_24487_en.jpg"
alt="St. Andrew's Building"
title="St. Andrew's Building"
class=""
style="width : 140px; height : 167px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " /> <br />The Faculty of Education is based in an award-winning building, providing you with a superb setting for your studies.</p>

</div>
<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.85286"></a>
<h1>Teaching in schools</h1>
<p>The Faculty of Education is one of the educational leaders in innovation in undergraduate teaching and learning with creative online support. It has one of the most comprehensive and significant departments of Adult &amp; Continuing Education in the UK with a strong international reputation. The faculty is ranked amongst the best worldwide for its community development work. </p>
<p>As well as developing educational thought, the Faculty of Education has a particular responsibility to prepare students for teaching in Catholic schools.</p>
<p>Undergraduate degrees leading to a qualification in teaching are:<br /></p>
<ul class="longlist"><li><a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/primaryeducation/">Bachelor of Education (BEd) with Honours (Primary)</a> </li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/primaryeducationwithteachingqualificationdumfriescampus/">Master of Arts (MA) in Education with Primary Teaching Qualification (Dumfries Campus)<br /></a></li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/secondary/religiousandphilosophicaleducation/">Master of Arts (MA) in Religious & Philosophical Education with Secondary Teaching Qualification</a> </li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/secondary/technologicaleducation/">Bachelor of Technological Education (BTechEd) (Secondary)</a> </li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/music/">Bachelor of Education in Music (BEd Music)</a> [taught jointly with the Royal Scottish Academy of Music &amp; Drama] (Primary and Secondary). </li></ul>
<p>Teaching qualification for graduates:</p>
<ul class="longlist"><li><a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/postgraduatediplomaineducationprimarysecondary/">Postgraduate Diploma in Education (Primary/Secondary)</a></li></ul>
<p>The faculty hosts the <a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/technologyandmanagement/">Joint Honours degree in Technology & Management</a> which is coordinated by the Robert Clark Centre for Technological Education in partnership with the Department of Management. It also offers a <a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/communitydevelopment/">BA Community Development</a> degree for students already working with adults in a community setting.</p>
<p>The faculty also offers a <a href="/departments/religiouseducation/coursesanddegreeprogrammes/certificateinreligiouseducationbydistancelearningcredl/">Certificate in Religious Education by Distance Learning</a> (CREDL) which is recognised by the Bishops of Scotland as a preliminary qualification in generalist Catholic Religious Education for students who wish to teach Religious Education in Catholic primary or secondary schools and who were unable to attend the Faculty of Education of the University of Glasgow. It can be completed concurrently with a BEd or PGDE course, or subsequently.</p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>

<a name="d.en.92885"></a>
<h1>Scottish Survey of Adult Literacy and Numeracy</h1>
<p><strong>Duration:</strong> October 2008 - December 2009</p>
<p><strong>Funder and Value:</strong> Scottish Government, &pound;450,000</p>
<p><strong>Abstract:</strong>&nbsp; The Faculty of Education at the University of Glasgow is leading a consortium to conduct a large-scale survey of the Scottish population to determine the level and distribution of literacy and numeracy skills. Our partners are the University of Edinburgh, the National Foundation for Educational Research and Gallup Europe. The funder for the research is the Education Analytical Services Division of the Scottish Government.</p>
<p>This is the first time the Scottish population has been surveyed since 1996, and the results will be comparable with the results of that survey as well as internationally. It provides an important opportunity to create a snapshot of the skills in Scotland and understand how those skill levels fit with other OECD countries.</p>
<p>The survey, of 2500 individuals in all parts of Scotland, will be conducted in early 2009, with results expected in October 2009.</p>
<p>For more information, please contact Principal Investigator Ralf St.Clair, <a href="mailto:rstclair@educ.gla.ac.uk">rstclair@educ.gla.ac.uk</a>.</p>

<a name="d.en.92305"></a>
<h1>Inter-life: Interoperability and Transition</h1>
<p><strong>Duration:</strong> 2008 - 2011</p>
<p><strong>Funder &amp; Value:</strong> ESRC / EPSRC: &pound;500,000</p>
<p><strong>Details: </strong>The project is investigating the use of Information and Communications Technologies (ICTs) to support skills development by young people to enhance their management of life transitions. It is developing a mobile and three-dimensional (3D) virtual community called 'Inter-Life'.&nbsp; Educational and social transitions have significant impacts on performance, motivation and identity formation.&nbsp; Inter-Life offers the opportunity for participants to work together on transition activities in the community, whether they are logged in, or using their mobile device away from the desktop.&nbsp; It&nbsp; provides reflective and personal development tools and scenarios for transitions, to demonstrate the flexibility and robustness of the educational and technical designs.&nbsp; In particular, the research focuses upon:</p>
<ul><li>User engagement, co-design, and development </li>
<li>Identification of learning outcomes, processes, and skills acquisition </li>
<li>Participant identity formation and development associated with Inter-Life usage </li>
<li>Professional development of educators working in 3D communities</li></ul>
<p>The project adopts mixed-method, technology-enhanced data gathering and analysis. Phenomenographic techniques are being used - analysing personal accounts of participants across a range of settings. The project is investigating identity development from an Activity Theory perspective, viewing identity as individual and social construct, rather than a fixed quality or 'given'.&nbsp; The project is possible because of the combined talents of our interdisciplinary team based at the Universities of Glasgow and Stirling, and also involving two highly respected expert consultants.</p>
<ul><li><a href="#glasgow">Project Team Members at the University of Glasgow</a> </li>
<li><a href="#stirling">Project Team Members at the University of Stirling </a></li>
<li href="#consultants"><a href="#consultants">Project Consultants (External)</a></li></ul>
<p></p>
<hr />
<h3>Project Team</h3>
<p><br />
<a name="glasgow"></a>University of Glasgow<br />Faculty of Education<br />St Andrews Building<br />11 Eldon Street<br />Glasgow G3 6NH</p>
<p><strong><a href="/faculties/education/staff/victorelally/">Vic Lally<br /></a>Project Director and Principal Investigator</strong></p>
<p><strong><a href="mailto:v.lally@educ.gla.ac.uk">v.lally@educ.gla.ac.uk</a></strong></p>
<p>Vic&nbsp;is the founding Director of the <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/stemed/">Interdisciplinary Centre for Research and Teaching in STEM Education</a> at the University of Glasgow.&nbsp; Vic's research interests in learning in technology-enhanced contexts include Computer Supported Collaborative Learning (CSCL) and learning in three-dimensional and mobile environments.&nbsp; He has written over 100 papers and articles, and been Director/co-director of 17 national and international projects, as well as editing/co-authoring 4 books.&nbsp; He has worked extensively in China and Europe, and is currently developing a collaborative professional development programme with colleagues in South Africa and Malawi.&nbsp; As Vic's latest project, 'Inter-Life' (ESRC/EPSRC â€“ 2008-2011 under the Technology Enhanced Learning Programme) is a key investigation of the learning of life transition skills by young people, using highly innovative three-dimensional online tools and environments, and a range of analytical techniques that he has researched and developed in an extensive research programme.</p>
<p><br />
<a href="/faculties/education/staff/janevmagill/"><strong>Jane Magill</strong> </a>
<br />
<strong>Co-investigator</strong></p>
<p><a href="mailto:j.magill@elec.gla.ac.uk">j.magill@elec.gla.ac.uk</a></p>
<p>Dr Jane Magill is Deputy Director of the <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/stemed/">Interdisciplinary Centre for Research and Teaching in STEM Education</a> and Director of the <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/rcc/index.html">Robert Clark Centre for Technological Education</a> at the University of Glasgow.&nbsp; A doctoral graduate in Chemical Physics from the University of Manchester, she has experience in academic and industrial research in materials science and semiconductor technology. She is involved in teaching and research in electrical engineering and more recently in STEM education, and is a lecturer in a degree programme for future technology teachers.&nbsp; Jane believes that public engagement in Science, Technology, Engineering and Maths (STEM) is vital and works with many organisations to develop this area. She is a science specialist at the NESTA/DfES sponsored &quot;Creative Science Teaching&quot; Labs run by PAL, <a href="http://www.pallabs.org">www.pallabs.org</a></p>
<p><br />
<strong><a href="/faculties/education/staff/briancanavan/">Brian Canavan<br /></a>Co-investigator</strong></p>
<p><a href="mailto:b.canavan@elec.gla.ac.uk">b.canavan@elec.gla.ac.uk</a></p>
<p>Dr Brian Canavan is a lecturer at the Robert Clark Centre for Technological Education at the University of Glasgow.&nbsp; An engineering designer for a number of years, working in various industrial sectors, including shipbuilding, pharmaceutical and petrochemicals, Brian subsequently studied at the University of Glasgow in both graduate and postgraduate capacities, culminating in his achieving a doctorate in Cognition and Educational Technology from the University's Faculty of Engineering. He has a range of experience in academic research including the evaluation of Information and Communication Technologies, problem-based-learning and reflective practice in learning.&nbsp; He also has a keen interest in issues relating to the development of the Technology and Science curriculum in Scotland and beyond and has published in a number of international conferences proceedings and journals. </p>
<p><br />
<strong>Steve Brindley<br />Co-investigator</strong></p>
<p><a href="mailto:s.brindley@physics.gla.ac.uk">s.brindley@physics.gla.ac.uk</a></p>
<p>Stephen Brindley is a research fellow with the Interdisciplinary Centre for Research and Teaching in STEM Education at the University of Glasgow.&nbsp; Steve originally trained as a geologist, obtaining degrees from London and Sheffield universities, with around 12 years experience in various research and industry roles, including 5 years as a senior geologist in a service company for the oil industry.&nbsp; Steve is particularly interested in designing and evaluating strategies for learning and developing innovative projects that use a variety of different media and activities.&nbsp; This includes using interactive handsets to research impact and understanding of audiences -from university students to public and school pupils.&nbsp; Steve also holds a PGCE in secondary school science from Keele University.&nbsp; For the past 11 years has worked as an informal science education professional creating and delivering memorable science learning experiences for children and adults of all ages.&nbsp; This includes a number of outreach projects, local and national competitions, teacher CPD events, summer courses, and school festivals and events in public places. Steve also managed SETPOINT (West of Scotland), which he helped to set up and was part of the team that organised the Glasgow University Science Festival.</p>
<p><br />
<strong>Jon Trinder</strong></p>
<p><strong>Technical developer and web manager</strong></p>
<p><a href="mailto:jont@elec.gla.ac.uk">jont@elec.gla.ac.uk</a></p>
<p>Jon is Chief Technician - Computing Support, in the Dept of Electronic and Electrical Engineering, having worked extensively in computing support across a wide range of industries and applications.&nbsp; Jon's Funded Projects have included work for the Higher Education Academy Engineering Subject Centre: Portable Learning and Assessment â€“ Towards Ubiquitous Education; University of Glasgow Chancellors Fund: handheld computer technologies to enhance access, flexibility, efficiency and effectiveness of course provision in higher education.</p>
<p></p>
<p><a href="#top">Top</a></p>
<p><strong></strong>Stirling FK9 4LA</p>
<p></p>
<p><a href="http://www.cs.stir.ac.uk/">Department of Computing Science and Mathematics</a> <br />
<a name="stirling"></a>University of Stirling<br /></p>
<p>Evan Magill<br />Institutional Principal Investigator</p>
<p><a href="mailto:ehm@cs.stir.ac.uk">ehm@cs.stir.ac.uk</a></p>
<p>Evan is a Professor within the Department of Computing Science and Mathematics at the University of Stirling. His research interests include Healthcare and Homecare, Wireless Sensor Networks, Home networks, Middleware, and Voice over IP.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Within Inter-life he will lead the work on integrating real devices, such as mobile phones, with devices in the virtual world.&nbsp; Currently Professor Magill is the institutional lead on the EPSRC funded project PAM. This project investigates the role of technology for the ambient monitoring of psychiatric patients at home. He is also an investigator in the SHEFC funded project MATCH. This studies the role of technology in assisting care in the home. He is an investigator with the EPSRC funded project. PROSEN. This is investigating wireless sensor networks within a wind farm setting. He is also the lead academic on a Knowledge Transfer Partnership (KTP) with Sysnet investigating the combination of P2P and mobiles technologies.</p>
<p>Professor Magill is a Chartered Engineer and a Fellow of the Institution of Engineering and Technology (previously IEE) . He holds a PhD from the University of Strathclyde.</p>
<p><strong>Mario Kolberg<br />Co-investigator</strong></p>
<p><a href="mailto:mko@cs.stir.ac.uk">mko@cs.stir.ac.uk</a></p>
<p>Mario is a lecturer within the Department of Computing Science and Mathematics at the University of Stirling. His research interests include Peer-to-Peer overlay networks, Home Automation, and IP Telephony.</p>
<p>Within Inter-life he is a co-investigator working on integrating real devices, such as mobile phones, with devices in the virtual world.&nbsp; Mario is also the academic supervisor in a Knowledge Transfer Partnership focusing on developing a Peer-to-Peer overlay for mobile handsets.&nbsp; Previously, he was leading a project funded by Panasonic (USA) investigating efficiency gains in structured Peer-to-Peer overlays.&nbsp; He is also a Co-Investigator in the MATCH project, focusing on integrating different network technologies for care in the home. He was leading an effort providing a proof-of-concept demonstrating the integration of digital pen and paper with networked appliances. He has been for extended research visits to Telcordia Technologies, NJ, USA, a leading presence in home automation, and Avaya Labs Research, NJ, USA, a leading internet telephony provider.</p>
<p>He is a Senior Member of the IEEE, and Co-Editor of the Feature Topic on Consumer Communication and Networking of the IEEE Communications Magazine.&nbsp; He holds a PhD from the University of Strathclyde.</p>
<p><a href="#top">Top</a></p>
<h4><a name="consultants"></a>
<hr />Project Consultants<br />
<a href="http://www.shef.ac.uk/education/staff/academic/pomerantz.html">Mike Pomerantz</a> (England)<br />
<a href="mailto:M.pomerantz@sheffield.ac.uk">M.pomerantz@sheffield.ac.uk</a></h4>
<p>Michael Pomerantz is a senior educational psychologist with Derbyshire County Council and an Associate Tutor to the Doctoral Programmes in Educational Psychology at the University of Sheffield. His research interests include supervision, able underachievers, gifted and talented pupils, vulnerable and marginalised pupils, &quot;hard to reach&quot; students, experiential training, social justice, racial equality and knowledge construction. He has taught abroad in the United States, Singapore, St. Lucia, Trinidad and Ireland.</p>
<p>He has accepted recent commissioned research consultancies from Belle Wallace who was the president of NACE (National Association for Able Children in Education) and from Capita to write training materials about Dual Exceptionality for the National Primary and Secondary Strategies. The former project involved a team of researchers in the gifted and talented (G + T) field conducting a series of interviews with G + T co-coordinators, senior managers, pupils, parents and governors at a selected group of London based schools.. The published summary is now likely to be published as a book.</p>
<p>Mike's contribution to the Inter-Life Project will be to coordinate a Derbyshire based Research Community of young people helping to consult about the design and testing of websites and to make a series of short video clips depicting socially skillful solutions to overcoming vulnerability.</p>
<h4>Maddy Sclater (Scotland)<br />
<a href="mailto:mfslater@googlemail.com">mfslater@googlemail.com</a></h4>
<p>Dr Madeleine Sclater has over twelve years' experience of researching at international level within the field of e-learning.&nbsp; Her current research is focused on developing and fostering creativity in professional learning within e-learning environments. Madeleine's professional work has involved extensive online teaching experience in Higher Education.&nbsp; She is currently engaged in the development of a new Masters level e-learning programme in Professional Development.&nbsp; She has worked with people across a wide range of disciplines (e.g. Art and Design, Social Work, Health, Product Design Engineering, Adult Education).&nbsp; In her work Madeleine has implemented novel pedagogical models, using Internet technologies, to support research and the advancement of creativity and innovation among academics, professional practitioners and learners. She holds an interdisciplinary PhD from the Digital Design Studio (DDS) at Glasgow School of Art and HATII (Humanities Advanced Technology And Information Institute) (2007) in the fields of Education, New Technology, and Art and Design.<br /></p>
<p></p>
<hr />
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
