<a name="d.en.72349"></a>
<h1>Does Religious Education Work?</h1>
<span lang="EN-GB"><h2>An Analysis of the Aims, Practices &amp; Models of Effectiveness in Religious Education across the UK</h2>
<p><strong>Research Project Summary</strong>
</p>
<p><strong>Duration:</strong>&nbsp;December 2007 - December 2010</p>
<p><strong>Funder and Value:</strong> Arts &amp; Humanities Research Councilâ€™s Religion and Society programme, &pound;365,326</p>
<p><strong>Abstract:</strong> This three-year project is the first major research project undertaken by the Centre for Studies in Faith, Culture and Education at Glasgow University. The project is funded by the Arts &amp; Humanities Research Councilâ€™s Religion and Society programme and is intended to create the single most comprehensive study to date of the state of religious education across the combined jurisdictions of the United Kingdom. </p>

<p>The study will unpack the various kinds of claims made with respect to Religious Education in the very different contexts of England and Wales, Northern Ireland and Scotland. Using a combination of philosophical, theological and detailed ethnographic approaches, we intend conducting a study of the local (school-focused) social, cultural and pedagogical practices which shape the delivery of Religious Education.<br />
<br /></p>
</span>
<ul class="longlist"><li><a href="/faculties/education/research/currentresearchprojects/doesreligioneducationwork/researchteam/">Research Team</a></li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/research/currentresearchprojects/doesreligioneducationwork/projectproposal/">Project Proposal</a></li>

<li><a href="/faculties/education/research/currentresearchprojects/doesreligioneducationwork/timetable/">Timetable</a></li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/research/currentresearchprojects/doesreligioneducationwork/publications/">Publications</a>
</li></ul>

<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.19643"></a>
<h1>Faculty of Education Research</h1>
<span><p>The Faculty of Education offers a dynamic environment for researchers and research students, with a strong network of national and international collaborative links. </p>
<p>The research profile of the Faculty benefits from the inclusion of researchers with expertise across all sectors of education- formal and non-formal, pre-school through to higher, adult, work based and community education. Across the Faculty there is a strong focus on research relating to the enhancement of teaching and learning and associated issues of access and social justice, with extensive collaboration with government bodies, employers, education authorities, schools, colleges, the voluntary sector, urban and rural regeneration agencies.</p>
<p>Staff within the Faculty belong to one of&nbsp;six specific Research and Knowledge Transfer Groups: </p>
<ul><li>Creativity, Culture and Faith</li>
<li>Interdisciplinary Science Education, Technologies and Learning (ISETL)</li>
<li>Leadership and Professional Learning</li>
<li>Lifelong Learning, Place and Engagement</li>
<li>Pedagogy, Policy and Practice</li>
<li>Social Inclusion and Global Injustice<p></p>
<hr /></li></ul>
<h2>Graduate School</h2>
<p>Our <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/"><span style="color: #333333;">Graduate School</span> </a>provides an excellent environment in which to pursue postgraduate research and training. It seeks to provide the widest possible range of opportunities for disciplinary, multidisciplinary and interdisciplinary postgraduate study.</p>
<p>For Graduate School enquiries please contact: <a href="mailto: M.Porch@admin.gla.ac.uk">Mrs M Porch</a>, Administrative Assistant, Room 425b, St Andrew's Building. Telephone:&nbsp; +44 (0)141-330 3021</p></span>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="twocolclear"></div></div></div>

<div class="maincontent" >
<a name="d.en.24483"></a>
<h1>About us</h1>
<p>The Faculty of Education is the most recently formed in the
University.&nbsp; Its roots, however, go back to the 19th Century founded as
it is on a teachersâ€™ college, one of the oldest and most established
departments of adult and lifelong learning in Britain and a number of
research and teaching centres, most especially Europeâ€™s long
established Scottish Centre for Research in Education (SCRE).<br />
<br />In keeping with the identity and ambition of a major international,
and research-led University the Faculty of Education offers
opportunities for those wishing to study with scholars of outstanding
international reputation.<br />
<br />Among the key areas of faculty strength are included:<br /></p>
<ul><li>Adult and Lifelong Learning, with a strong commitment to Community Education</li>
<li>Professional Knowledge in Teachersâ€™ Education</li>
<li>Science, Technology and Informatics</li>
<li>Culture, Religion and Education</li>
<li>Assessment and Learning in Education including Support for Learning, and Able Pupils</li>
<li>Teacher Education.<br /></li></ul>
<p>Our extensive and continually evolving postgraduate programmes
include an innovative on-line doctorate in education as well as Masters
degrees, including professionally focused qualifications in Educational
Practice, and a number of named pathways in Adult Education; Support
for Learning; Curriculum; English Language Teaching; Religion and
Education.&nbsp; <br />
<br />A particular strength of the Faculty is educational leadership
where we offer a number of programmes including our ground-breaking
Masters in Educational and Public Service Leadership taught in
collaboration with the Universityâ€™s Business School.&nbsp; Complementing
this is a programme designed particularly for those who wish to become
leaders in religiously denominated schools.&nbsp; We also offer a Masters in
Educational Research.<br />
<br />As a research-led Faculty of Education we are constantly re-shaping
and developing our teacher education programmes which include a
Bachelor of Education; Professional Graduate Diploma in Education
(Secondary); Professional Graduate Diploma in Education (Primary); MA
in Philosophical and Religious Education; Bachelor of Technological
Education and a Bachelor of Education (Music) taught in collaboration
with the Royal Scottish Academy of Music and Drama.<br />
<br />The work of the Faculty is organised around four departments (<a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/adulteducation/index.html">Adult
and Continuing Education</a>; <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/faculties/education_nowt4/depts/cstudies/index.shtml">Curriculum Studies</a>; <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/educationalstudies/">Educational Studies</a>;
<a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/departments/religiouseducation/">Religious Education</a>) and a number of research and development centres
(<a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/centres/cradall/index.shtml">CRADALL</a>; <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/centres/scienceeducation/">Centre for Science Education</a>; <a href="http://www.gla.ac.uk/rcc/index.html">Robert Clark Centre for
Technological Education</a> and <a href="http://www.scre.ac.uk/">SCRE</a>).&nbsp; Colleagues across the Faculty offer
a wide range of research and professional consultancy as well as
Continuing Professional Development.<br />
<br />Please enjoy browsing our website and feel free to contact any of my colleagues who will be only too happy to help.<br />
<br />I am sure that you will find the information useful and hope that
we can welcome you on one of our many exciting undergraduate or
postgraduate courses.<br />
<br />
<strong>James C Conroy<br />Dean</strong></p>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />

<a name="d.en.19507"></a>
<h1>Partnerships</h1>
<p>As a substantial Faculty in one of the world's top 100 universities, we enjoy collaborations with colleagues in Scotland, UK and around the world. Our strong and dynamic relationships with policy makers and practitioners afford access to the educational community as a whole so that we can conduct our scholarship, carry out our research and disseminate our findings to best effect.</p>
<p>Information on </p>
<ul class="longlist"><li><a href="/faculties/education/partnerships/school/">School partnership</a> </li>
<li><a href="/faculties/education/partnerships/community/">Community partnership</a> </li>
<li>Research partnership<br /></li></ul>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />  
</div>
<div class="onecolclear"></div></div></div>

<a name="d.en.9795"></a>
<h1>Faculty of Education</h1>
<p>The Faculty of Education at the University of Glasgow is an exciting and stimulating place to study at both <a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/">undergraduate</a> and <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/">postgraduate</a> levels. New degree programmes include: <a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/primaryeducation/">BEd Honours in Primary Education</a>; the <a href="/faculties/education/teachinginschools/primary/primaryeducationwithteachingqualificationdumfriescampus/">MA in Primary Education</a> offered on the Dumfries campus; the <a href="/faculties/education/programmesandcourses/undergraduatestudy/childhoodpractice/">BA in Childhood Practice</a>; and the <a href="/faculties/education/graduateschool/taughtprogrammes/pgde/">PGDE one-year programme for primary and secondary education</a> which offers 90 Masters-level credits. It has a robust, active and expanding <a href="/faculties/education/research/">research</a> portfolio with international expertise in the areas of Adult and Lifelong Learning, Science Education, Teacher Education, Religion and Education, Social Justice and Globalisation and Education among others.</p>
<p>We will be pleased to hear from you and welcome your interest in the Faculty of Education at the University of Glasgow.</p>

<a name="d.en.128796"></a>
<h1>Two in a row</h1>
<p id="issuedate"><strong>Issued: Tue, 01 Sep 2009 14:38:00 BST</strong></p>
<p>Mr Iain Houston, an alumnus of the University and holder of the Postgraduate Certificate of Education from the Faculty of Education in 2004-05, beat very stiff competition to be awarded the accolade of Scottish Teacher of the Year at the 2009 Scottish Education Awards.&nbsp; He is the second Glasgow University Faculty of Education student to have been in receipt of the award in as many years, following last yearâ€™s winner, David Miller who also claimed the UK Teacher of the Year Award.</p>
<p>Ian who is a physics teacher at St Joseph's College in Dumfries impressed the judges with his original approach to teaching, which included the use of Dr Who and science from 19th century experiments.</p>
<p>Ian said, â€œI would like to give the University my thanks for stimulating my own intellectual and pedagogical development. I thoroughly enjoyed my year in the Faculty of Education and am particularly grateful for the support and guidance of my physics and maths lecturers, Elizabeth Aitkenhead and Willie Magill.&nbsp; I would be delighted to return to the Faculty and give something back in the form of workshops to the PGDE students.â€</p>
<p>We are delighted with Ianâ€™s success and wish him every success in the forthcoming awards in London for UK Teacher of the Year where he will be flying the flag for Scotland.</p>
<p>Professor James C Conroy<br />Dean </p>

<div class="maincontent">
<h1>Latest news</h1>
<div class="newsfeatureswide">
<h1><a href="/faculties/education/newsandevents/news/">Faculty news</a></h1>
<h2><img src="/media/media_123643_en-70x50.jpg"
alt="Scottish Education Awards"
title="Scottish Education Awards"
class=""
style="width : 70px; height : 50px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " />Two in a row
</h2>
<p>Mr Iain Houston, an alumnus of the University and holder of the Postgraduate Certificate of Education from the Faculty of Education in 2004-05, beat very stiff competition to be awarded the accolade of Scottish Teacher of the Year at the 2009 Scottish Education Awards.</p>
<h2><img src="/media/media_127654_en-70x50.gif"
alt="sounds like science"
title="sounds like science"
class=""
style="width : 70px; height : 50px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " />Scottish Government funding award for Science Engagement
</h2>
<p>The Faculty of Education has won an award from Scottish Government's Science Engagement Scheme. 'Science and Creativity, an exploration through art' will enable teenagers to explore the importance of creativity in science through discussion and project workshops with scientists and musicians.</p>
<h2><img src="/media/media_127094_en-70x50.gif"
alt="national student survey logo"
title="national student survey logo"
class=""
style="width : 70px; height : 50px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " />Faculty achieves 92% student satisfaction in NSS survey
</h2>
<p>Academics in the Faculty of Education have been working hard to ensure that our teacher education programmes are amongst the very best in Britain.  This year has seen us achieve a 92% satisfaction rating from our teacher education graduates (one of the highest scores in the UK).</p>

</div>
<br style="font-size:1px; line-height: 0; height: 0; clear:right;" />
</div>


<div class="maincontent">
<h1>Latest events</h1>
<div class="newsfeatureswide">
<h1><a href="/faculties/education/newsandevents/events/">Faculty events</a></h1>
<h2><img src="/media/media_129029_en-70x50.jpg"
alt="Openday Sep 2009"
title="Openday Sep 2009"
class=""
style="width : 70px; height : 50px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " />Open Day 2009
</h2>
<p>The University of Glasgow Open Days allow prospective undergraduate students to speak to staff in academic departments, find out more about courses, tour the facilities, visit student accommodation and see what life would be like as a student at Glasgow. </p>
<h2><img src="/media/media_126269_en-70x50.jpg"
alt=""
title=""
class=""
style="width : 70px; height : 50px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " />Rt Hon Charles Kennedy MP to deliver Stanley Nisbet Educational Colloquium Lecture 2009
</h2>
<p>This yearâ€™s lecture will be delivered by the Rt Hon Charles Kennedy MP, Rector of the University of Glasgow, and is entitled â€œEducation in the New Political Landscape of Scotlandâ€.
</p>
<h2><img src="/media/media_126268_en-70x50.jpg"
alt="Students talking in the St Andrew's Building"
title="Students talking in the St Andrew's Building"
class=""
style="width : 70px; height : 50px; border : ; padding : ; margin : ; float : ;  " />Postgraduate Open Evening for Adult Education Programmes
</h2>
<p>The Department of Adult & Continuing Education is holding an Open Evening for it's postgraduate programmes on Thursday 16 July 2009. The evening will run from 6.30pm to 8.00pm in room 433, St Andrew's Building.
Please come along!
</p>
